envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n     4→\n     5→import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n     6→import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n     7→import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n     8→import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n     9→import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n    10→\n    11→import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n    12→import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n    13→\n    14→import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n    15→import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n    16→\n    17→option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n    18→option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n    19→option java_multiple_files = true;\n    20→option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n    21→option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n    22→\n    23→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    24→// External Processing Filter\n    25→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    26→\n    27→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    28→\n    29→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    30→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    31→//\n    32→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    33→\n    34→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    35→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    36→//\n    37→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    39→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    40→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    41→//\n    42→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    43→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    44→// and how it should be processed.\n    45→//\n    46→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    47→//\n    48→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    49→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    50→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    51→//   sent asynchronously.\n    52→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    53→//\n    54→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    55→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    56→// processor must send a matching response.\n    57→//\n    58→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    59→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    60→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    61→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    62→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    63→//   to SEND.\n    64→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    65→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    66→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    67→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    68→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    69→//   request trailers.\n    70→//\n    71→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    72→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    73→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    74→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    75→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    76→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    77→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    78→//\n    79→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    80→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    81→//\n    82→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    83→//   on the content of the headers.\n    84→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    85→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    86→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    87→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    88→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    89→//\n    90→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    91→// server\n    92→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    93→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    94→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    95→//\n    96→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    97→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    98→// name.\n    99→//\n   100→// [#next-free-field: 18]\n   101→message ExternalProcessor {\n   102→  reserved 4;\n   103→\n   104→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   105→\n   106→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   107→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   108→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   109→\n   110→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   111→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   112→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   113→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   114→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   115→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   116→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   117→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   118→\n   119→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   120→  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n   121→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n   122→\n   123→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   124→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   125→  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n   126→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n   127→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   128→  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n   129→\n   130→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   131→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   132→  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n   133→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   134→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   135→  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n   136→\n   137→  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n   138→  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n   139→  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n   140→  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n   141→  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n   142→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   143→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   144→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   145→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   146→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   147→    gte {}\n   148→  }];\n   149→\n   150→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. = \"proto3\";\n\npackage envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n\nimport \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n\nimport \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\noption (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 18]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n    // definition for safe parsing.\n    repeated string typed = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n  // the external processing server.\n  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n}\n\n// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n//\n// This works as below:\n//\n//   1. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\nmessage HeaderForwardingRules {\n  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n\n  // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n}\n\n// Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n// virtual host or cluster.\nmessage ExtProcPerRoute {\n  oneof override {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n    // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n    bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n\n    // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n  }\n}\n\n// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n// [#next-free-field: 8]\nmessage ExtProcOverrides {\n  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n  bool async_mode = 2;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n\n  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n  // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\n  // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\n\n  // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\n  // service. \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n    22→option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n    23→\n    24→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    25→// External Processing Filter\n    26→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    27→\n    28→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    29→\n    30→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    31→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    32→//\n    33→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    34→\n    35→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    36→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    37→//\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    39→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    40→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    41→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    42→//\n    43→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    44→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    45→// and how it should be processed.\n    46→//\n    47→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    48→//\n    49→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    50→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    51→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    52→//   sent asynchronously.\n    53→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    54→//\n    55→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    56→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    57→// processor must send a matching response.\n    58→//\n    59→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    60→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    61→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    62→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    63→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    64→//   to SEND.\n    65→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    66→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    67→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    68→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    69→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    70→//   request trailers.\n    71→//\n    72→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    73→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    74→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    75→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    76→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    77→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    78→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    79→//\n    80→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    81→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    82→//\n    83→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    84→//   on the content of the headers.\n    85→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    86→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    87→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    88→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    89→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    90→//\n    91→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    92→// server\n    93→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    94→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    95→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    96→//\n    97→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    98→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    99→// name.\n   100→//\n   101→// [#next-free-field: 20]\n   102→message ExternalProcessor {\n   103→  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n   104→  // is received in response to request headers.\n   105→  enum RouteCacheAction {\n   106→    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n   107→    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   108→    // field is set in an external processor response.\n   109→    DEFAULT = 0;\n   110→\n   111→    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   112→    // the external processor response.\n   113→    CLEAR = 1;\n   114→\n   115→    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   116→    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n   117→    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n   118→    // to true.\n   119→    RETAIN = 2;\n   120→  }\n   121→\n   122→  reserved 4;\n   123→\n   124→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   125→\n   126→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   127→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   128→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   129→\n   130→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   131→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   132→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   133→  // error downstream. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 20]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n    // field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n  // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n  // received in response to request headers. Currently, the deferred stream closure\n  // is only used in :ref:`observability_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`.\n  // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client to\n  // backend stream lifetime. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\n  // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n    // while trailers are skipped.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Send the header or trailer.\n    SEND = 1;\n\n    // Do not send the header or trailer.\n    SKIP = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n  // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n  // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n  // to be set correctly:\n  // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n  // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n  // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n  //\n  // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n  // encoding whenever feasible. This is the default.\n    NONE = 0;\n\n    // Stream the body to the server in pieces as they arrive at the\n    // proxy.\n    STREAMED = 1;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body at once.\n    // If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the\n    // downstream system will receive an error.\n    BUFFERED = 2;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body in one\n    // chunk. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n    10→it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n    11→and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n    12→\n    13→The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n    24→that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n    25→stream requests from the proxy.\n    26→\n    27→This filter is a work in progress. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\nbe found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n\nStatistics\n----------\nThis filter outputs statistics in the\n``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. Security fixes typically happen\n    20→quarterly as well, but this depends on the number and severity of security bugs. Other releases\n    21→are ad-hoc and best-effort.\n    22→\n    23→### Security releases\n    24→\n    25→Critical security fixes are owned by the Envoy security team, which provides fixes for the\n    26→`main` branch. Once those fixes are ready, the maintainers\n    27→of stable releases backport them to the remaining supported stable releases.\n    28→\n    29→### Backports\n    30→\n    31→All other security and reliability fixes can be nominated for backporting to stable releases\n    32→by Envoy maintainers, Envoy security team, the change author, or members of the Envoy community\n    33→by adding the `backport/review` or `backport/approved` label (this can be done using [repokitteh]'s\n    34→`/backport` command). Changes nominated by the change author and/or members of the Envoy community\n    35→are evaluated for backporting on a case-by-case basis, and require approval from either the release\n    36→manager of stable release, Envoy maintainers, or Envoy security team. Once approved, those fixes\n    37→are backported from the `main` branch to all supported stable branches by the maintainers of\n    38→stable releases. New stable versions from non-critical security fixes are released on a regular\n    39→schedule, initially aiming for the bi-weekly releases.\n    40→\n    41→### Release management\n    42→\n    43→Major releases are handled by the maintainer on-call and do not involve any backports.\n    44→The details are outlined in the \"Cutting a major release\" section below.\n    45→Security releases are handled by a Release Manager and a Fix Lead. release\n   100→\n   101→* Take a look at open issues tagged with the current release, by\n   102→  [searching](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues) for\n   103→  \"is:open is:issue milestone:[current milestone]\" and either hold off until\n   104→  they are fixed or bump them to the next milestone.\n   105→* Begin marshalling the ongoing PR flow in this repo. Ask maintainers to hold off merging any\n   106→  particularly risky PRs until after the release is tagged. This is because we aim for main to be\n   107→  at release candidate quality at all times.\n   108→* Do a final check of the [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml):\n   109→  * Make any needed corrections (grammar, punctuation, formatting, etc.).\n   110→  * Check to see if any security/stable version release notes are duplicated in\n   111→    the major version release notes. These should not be duplicated.\n   112→  * Switch the repo to \"release\" mode by running `bazel run @envoy_repo//:release`. This tool\n   113→    will create a commit with the necessary changes for a release.\n   114→  * Update the [RELEASES](RELEASES.md) doc with the relevant dates. Now, or after you cut the\n   115→    release, please also make sure there's a stable maintainer signed up for next quarter,\n   116→    and the deadline for the next release is documented in the release schedule.\n   117→  * Get a review and merge.\n   118→* Create a pull request with that commit and **wait for tests to pass**.\n   119→* Once the tests have passed, and the PR has landed, CI will automatically create the tagged release and corresponding release branch.\n   120→* Switch the repo back to \"dev\" mode by running `bazel run @envoy_repo//:dev`. This tool will create a commit with the\n   121→  necessary changes to continue development.\n   122→* Create a pull request with that commit.\n   123→* Run the deprecate_versions.py script (`bazel run //tools/deprecate_version:deprecate_version`)\n   124→* If you haven't done this before, request posting permission from admins for all the groups in the next bullet.\n   125→* Craft a witty/uplifting email and send it to all the email aliases:\n   126→envoy-announce@googlegroups.com\n   127→envoy-users@googlegroups.com\n   128→envoy-dev@googlegroups.com\n   129→envoy-maintainers@googlegroups.com -\n   130→include in this email a link to the latest [release page](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases) (ending in `tag/[version]`)\n   131→* Announce in [#envoy-dev](https://envoyproxy.slack.com/archives/C78HA81DH) and [#envoy-users](https://envoyproxy.slack.com/archives/C78M4KW76) slack channels.\n   132→\n   133→## Security release schedule\n   134→\n   135→Security releases are published on a 3-monthly cycle, around the mid point between major releases.\n   136→\n   137→| Quarter |  Expected  |   Actual   | Difference |\n   138→|:-------:|:----------:|:----------:|:----------:|\n   139→| 2024 Q2 | 2024/06/04 | 2024/06/04 |   0 days   |\n   140→| 2024 Q3 | 2024/09/03 |\n   141→\n   142→NOTE: Zero-day vulnerabilities, and upstream vulnerabilities disclosed to us under embargo, may necessitate an emergency release with little or no warning.\n   143→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Security fixes typically happen\nquarterly as well, but this depends on the number and severity of security bugs. Other releases\nare ad-hoc and best-effort.\n\n### Security releases\n\nCritical security fixes are owned by the Envoy security team, which provides fixes for the\n`main` branch. Once those fixes are ready, the maintainers\nof stable releases backport them to the remaining supported stable releases.\n\n### Backports\n\nAll other security and reliability fixes can be nominated for backporting to stable releases\nby Envoy maintainers, Envoy security team, the change author, or members of the Envoy community\nby adding the `backport/review` or `backport/approved` label (this can be done using [repokitteh]'s\n`/backport` command). Changes nominated by the change author and/or members of the Envoy community\nare evaluated for backporting on a case-by-case basis, and require approval from either the release\nmanager of stable release, Envoy maintainers, or Envoy security team. Once approved, those fixes\nare backported from the `main` branch to all supported stable branches by the maintainers of\nstable releases. New stable versions from non-critical security fixes are released on a regular\nschedule, initially aiming for the bi-weekly releases.\n\n### Release management\n\nMajor releases are handled by the maintainer on-call and do not involve any backports.\nThe details are outlined in the \"Cutting a major release\" section below.\nSecurity releases are handled by a Release Manager and a Fix Lead. The Release Manager is\nresponsible for approving and merging backports, with responsibilties outlined\nin [BACKPORTS.md](BACKPORTS.md).\nThe Fix Lead is a member of the security\nteam and is responsible for coordinating the overall release. This includes identifying\nissues to be fixed in the release, communications with the Envoy community, and the\nactual mechanics of the release itself.\n\n| Quarter |       Release Manager with the current release, by\n  [searching](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues) for\n  \"is:open is:issue milestone:[current milestone]\" and either hold off until\n  they are fixed or bump them to the next milestone.\n* Begin marshalling the ongoing PR flow in this repo. Ask maintainers to hold off merging any\n  particularly risky PRs until after the release is tagged. This is because we aim for main to be\n  at release candidate quality at all times.\n* Do a final check of the [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml):\n  * Make any needed corrections (grammar, punctuation, formatting, etc.).\n  * Check to see if any security/stable version release notes are duplicated in\n    the major version release notes. These should not be duplicated.\n  * Switch the repo to \"release\" mode by running `bazel run @envoy_repo//:release`. This tool\n    will create a commit with the necessary changes for a release.\n  * Update the [RELEASES](RELEASES.md) doc with the relevant dates. Now, or after you cut the\n    release, please also make sure there's a stable maintainer signed up for next quarter,\n    and the deadline for the next release is documented in the release schedule.\n  * Get a review and merge.\n* Create a pull request with that commit and **wait for tests to pass**.\n* Once the tests have passed, and the PR has landed, CI will automatically create the tagged release and corresponding release branch.\n* Switch the repo back to \"dev\" mode by running `bazel run @envoy_repo//:dev`. This tool will create a commit with the\n  necessary changes to continue development.\n* Create a pull request with that commit.\n* Run the deprecate_versions.py script (`bazel run //tools/deprecate_version:deprecate_version`)\n* If you haven't done this before, request posting permission from admins for all the groups in the next bullet.\n* Craft a witty/uplifting email and send it to all the email aliases:\nenvoy-announce@googlegroups.com\nenvoy-users@googlegroups.com\nenvoy-dev@googlegroups.com\nenvoy-maintainers@googlegroups.com -\ninclude in this email a link to the latest [release page](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases) (ending in `tag/[version]`)\n* Announce in [#envoy-dev](https://envoyproxy.slack.com/archives/C78HA81DH) and [#envoy-users](https://envoyproxy.slack.com/archives/C78M4KW76) slack channels.\n\n## Security release schedule\n\nSecurity releases are published on a 3-monthly cycle, around the mid point between major releases.\n\n| Quarter |  Expected  |   Actual   | Difference |\n|:-------:|:----------:|:----------:|:----------:|\n| 2024 Q2 | 2024/06/04 | 2024/06/04 |   0 days   |\n| 2024 Q3 | 2024/09/03 |\n\nNOTE: Zero-day vulnerabilities, and upstream vulnerabilities disclosed to us under embargo, may necessitate an emergency release with little or no warning.\n","numLines":143,"startLine":1,"totalLines":143}}}
